## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (ordinary differential equation rate laws)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a concentration A, which is the standard dependent variable in chemical kinetics. With only (t, A) available, the most likely relationships are mass-action decay/production terms in A, possibly with time-varying rate coefficients or reversible/auto-catalytic effects expressed as ODE rate laws.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order rate law (constant-rate consumption/production): dA_dt = c0 (e.g., surface-catalyzed or saturated regime where rate is independent of A)
- First-order decay (unimolecular or pseudo-first-order): dA_dt = -c0 * A (radioactive/thermal decomposition; dilution-free exponential decay)
- Second-order decay (bimolecular with identical reactant): dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (2A -> products under mass-action kinetics)
- Nth-order power-law (empirical or complex mechanism lumping): dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (generalized mass-action/phenomenological kinetics)
- Linear sourceâ€“sink (production plus first-order loss): dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (constant inflow/formation with first-order removal)
- Reversible first-order approach to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (relaxation to equilibrium concentration c1)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-type mass-action (self-accelerating with limiting capacity): dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (A promotes its own formation but is limited by depletion/capacity)
- Product inhibition via rational damping (effective rate reduced at high A): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (crowding/inhibition-like slowdown without explicit second species)
- Time-varying first-order rate coefficient (e.g., changing conditions): dA_dt = -A * (c0 + c1 * t) (rate constant ramps approximately linearly in time)
- Exponentially relaxing rate coefficient (activation/deactivation of catalyst over time): dA_dt = -c0 * A * (1 + c1 * exp(-c2 * t)) (transient acceleration/slowdown)
- Periodic forcing of rate coefficient (external modulation): dA_dt = -c0 * A * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (light/chopping/periodic temperature or feed modulation)
- Stretched-exponentialâ€“like effective kinetics (heterogeneous environment proxy): dA_dt = -c0 * t**c1 * A (time-dependent hazard rate producing non-exponential decay)
- Composite parallel pathways (two loss channels with different orders): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (simultaneous unimolecular and bimolecular consumption)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Mass-action signature: dependence purely on A as A, A**2, A**n strongly suggests elementary unimolecular/bimolecular or lumped-order kinetics.
- Sign constraint: if A is being consumed, dA_dt should be negative for A > 0; if production dominates, dA_dt can be positiveâ€”checking sign vs A helps distinguish decay vs source terms.
- Equilibrium relaxation: terms of the form -(A - c) imply convergence to a steady-state concentration (fixed point) rather than decay to zero.
- Mechanism superposition: sums like -(c0*A + c1*A**2) indicate parallel reaction channels; dominance can switch with concentration (linear dominates at low A, quadratic at high A).
- Autocatalysis indicator: a factor A multiplying a growth term (e.g., A*(c - A)) implies self-acceleration at low A with eventual self-limitation and a nonzero steady state.
- Time-dependent environment: explicit t in the rate coefficient (e.g., (c0 + c1*t) or exp(-c*t)) indicates changing operating conditions (catalyst deactivation, temperature drift, feed changes) even without additional species variables.
- Periodic modulation: sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) in a multiplicative rate factor suggests externally forced kinetics; leads to oscillations in dA_dt even if A is monotone on average.
- Inhibition/crowding proxy: rational damping A/(1 + c*A) produces near-first-order behavior at low A and reduced incremental rate at high A, mimicking saturation/inhibition without introducing extra reactants.
- Identifiability caution: with only (t, A), different mechanisms can fit similarly (e.g., time-varying first-order vs mixed-order); prefer structures consistent with known chemistry and expected steady states.
